Long, Huey P. Radio Address, 1935 (transcript)	Long, Huey Pierce	1935				Long, Huey Pierce, 1893-1935.; Radio addresses, debates, etc.	Huey P. Long was elected governor of Louisiana in 1928.  Two years later he was elected to the U.S. Senate.  He continued to influence the state through his chosen successor, O, K. Allen.  In 1934, Long’s own presidential ambitions and his more radical social platform led him to break with President Franklin D. Roosevelt and form an alternative political organization, the Share-Our-Wealth Society.  Through the society, he advocated redistributing wealth through sharply graduated income and inheritance taxes. He found a ready and sympathetic audience for his ideas in Depression-era Americans.  Long effectively used radio to distribute his populist message.  This transcript is from a 1935 broadcast by Long. He was assassinated the same year. Book of Hours		c. 1430	1429; 1431; 15th Century				Teams of scribes and artists worked to produce the illuminated Book of Hours on vellum.  This great treasure, donated to the LSU Libraries by John S. McIlhenny to serve as its ceremonial 2 millionth volume, dates from the 1430s.  Created in northern France or possibly in Paris, it is written on 163 leaves of fine vellum (a term commonly used for the highest quality of parchment) in a gothic book hand and illustrated with 12 miniatures, elaborate decorated borders, and many fine initial letters illuminated in colors and gold.  The miniatures depict biblical scenes, but they also reflect contemporary life in the mid-fifteenth century.	Manuscript on vellum, in a gothic bookhand.  8vo (196 x 140 mm.) 163 folios.  From the library of the Pasquier family of Paris. Four Gospels of the Lord Jesus Christ according to the Authorized version of King James I		1931		Waltham Saint Lawrence, Berkshire: Golden Cockerel Press	decorations by Eric Gill		One of the most beautiful books printed in the 20th century is Eric Gill's edition of the Four Gospels. Printed at the Golden Cockerel Press in 1931, Gill's work was issued in an edition of 500 copies.  Gill (1882-1940) was a philosopher, sculptor, and type designer, whose beautiful Perpetua type is frequently used today.  His skill in matching and interweaving type with illustration was at its peak in the Four Gospels. Musurgia Universalis sive Ars Magna	Kircher, Athanasius	1650		Romae: Ex typographia Hæredum Francisci Corbelletti		Music	The elaborately engraved title page is fascinating for its symbolism.  The top section is dominated by a triangle symbolizing the Holy Trinity, with nine angelic choirs singing a canon on the words "Sanctus, sanctus, sanctus" (holy, holy, holy). The middle section contains secular symbolism: a female figure seated on a globe holds the lyre of Apollo and the panpipes of Marsyas, musical rivals who were judged by the Muses.     The lowest part of the picture shows blacksmiths in a cave: the sound of blacksmiths hammering led the Greek philosopher Pythagoras to important conclusions about musical pitch.  Pythagoras points to the blacksmiths and holds an illustration of his theorem, also using triangles, and hence referring obliquely once again to the Trinity at the top of the picture.	A Jesuit polymath, Athanasius Kircher (1602-1680) published more than 30 books on subjects ranging from China to Egypt to music.  Musurgia is his most influential work and was a source for almost every later German music theorist until well into the 18th century.  It is still considered essential to an understanding of 17th-century music and music theory. First Six Books of The Elements of Euclid in Which Coloured Diagrams and Symbols Are Used Instead of Letters for the Greater Ease of Learners	Oliver Byrne	1847		London: William Pickering		Mathematics; Geometry	In 1847, noted English publisher William Pickering brought out an unusual edition of Euclid edited by an otherwise unknown mathematician named Oliver Byrne.  The book's startlingly modern diagrams make an interesting contrast with the elegant but very Victorian criblé initials that decorate the typography.Byrne's edition covers the first 6 books of Euclid's Elements of Geometry, which range through most of elementary plane geometry and the theory of proportions. The striking diagrams are the result of Byrne's attempts to present Euclid's proofs in pictures, using as little text - and in particular as few labels - as possible.		en			E. A. Description de la Louisiane, nouvellement decouverte au sud'oüest de la Nouvelle France, par ordre du roy	Hennepin, Louis  (1640-1705)	1683		A Paris: Chez Amable Auroy		Indians of North America--Mississippi River Valley; Louisiana--Description and travel; Mississippi River--Discovery and exploration; Mississippi River Valley--History--To 1803	Louis Hennepin, a Recollet Friar (member of an order of reformed Franciscans), arrived in New France in 1675.  After spending four years as an itinerant missionary, Hennepin joined an expedition of the great French explorer Robert Cavalier, Sieur de la Salle, intent on probing the Mississippi. Hennepin and two companions ventured up the Mississippi as far as the Falls of St. Anthony (the site of Minneapolis), and returned to the Great Lakes by an alternate route.<br><br>In 1683, Hennepin published an account of his adventures, Description de la Louisiane.  An immediate best-seller, the book went through numerous editions and was one of the most widely read first-hand descriptions of New France.  The map that accompanies the volume, entitled "Carte de la Nouvelle France et de la Louisiane Nouvellement découverte," makes it the first cartographic appearance of Louisiana as a place-name. Cover										Kate Chopin (1851-1904) published Bayou Folk in 1894.  It was her second book, and her first to be commercially published.  Although today Chopin is considered among the most important women in nineteenth-century American fiction, she was a highly controversial writer during her lifetime. Her novel, The Awakening, published in 1899, brought Chopin critical abuse and public denunciation as an immoralist, and she consequently abandoned writing.  More recent critics call it a masterpiece of its time, significant for its social and psychological themes.  Special Collections recently acquired a copy of Bayou Folk, in which Chopin has written out and signed a variant version of her poem, “White Oaks,” substituting “live oaks” for “white oaks”:  Of all the places on earth I know I’d rather stay where the live oaks grow. From dawn till night, the whole day long They sing their musical, mystical song Of rest, rest for the time is flying, Dream, dream for the day is dying! Oh! That tomorrow were far away And all forever a long today When the world stands still and the soft winds blow In the beautiful land where the live oaks grow!  Although Chopin biographer Emily Toth suspects that the author inscribed more than one copy of this book, no others inscribed by her are known to survive, perhaps because the book was not made from sturdy materials.  In fact, LSU's copy is so fragile that the originals cannot safely be displayed. Tractor gals	Spell, Viela	1920					Viela Spell lived and photographed scenes in Crowley, Louisiana, in Acadia Parish. When she began taking photographs in the 1920s the art of photography was no longer exclusive to professionals. Kodak had introduced the first disposable camera in the late 1880s with the advertising line, "You push the button, we do the rest." Anyone with enough money to buy a preloaded camera and pay for for printing could take up the hobby. Although not professional photographs, these images serve to document various aspects of Louisiana history that might otherwise have gone unrecorded. Nestling ivory-billed woodpecker and J.J. Kuhn, March 6, 1938.	Tanner, James T.	1938				Bird watching; Woodpeckers; Tensas River National Wildlife Refuge (La.)--Photographs	James Taylor Tanner was born in Homer, New York, on March 6, 1914. He attended Cornell University and worked under Arthur A. Allen throughout the course of his graduate study. Tanner's master's thesis was titled "Sound Recording for a Natural History Museum." His Ph.D. dissertation, "Life History and Ecology of the Ivory-billed Woodpecker," was based on 21 months of field studies in the Singer tract in northeastern Louisiana, the last refuge for this nearly extinct species. In 1942 the National Audubon Society published Tanner's dissertation as "Research report number 1: The Ivory-billed Woodpecker."  The images presented here were taken by Tanner while on field study expeditions in Louisiana during the years 1935 to 1940. The Anatomy of Plants. With An idea of a philosophical history of plants, and Several other lectures, read before the Royal Society.	Grew, Nehemiah	1682		W. Rawlins [London]		Botany--Anatomy--Early works to 1800; Botany--England--Early works to 1800; Plants, Useful--England--Early works to 1800; Woody plants--England--Early works to 1800; Plant anatomy	The training in animal anatomy that English physician Nehemiah Grew (1641-1712) received stood him in good stead when he began investigating the anatomy of plants, as did his skill with a microscope, a relatively new invention at that time.  Grew's first book on plant anatomy, The Anatomy of Vegetables Begun, was presented to the Royal Society of London in 1672. The Anatomy of Plants (1682), his best known work, is particularly remembered for its discussion of sexual reproduction in plants, which was a new idea at the time.  The book is illustrated with beautiful engravings that represent the three-dimensional, microscopic structure of plant tissues.		en		Special Delivery: A Showcase of LSU Libraries Special Collections	E. Liriodendron tulipifera L., Tulip Poplar	Stones, Margaret	1976				Botanical illustration--Louisiana.;  Watercolor painting--Louisiana.;  Botanical artists--Australia.	The tulip poplar is widespread in the eastern United States and is used for interior finishing and cabinetry.  Pioneers used it for building, as well, despite the softness of the wood.  A handsome ornamental with attractive leaves and flowers, it is relatively fast growing and becomes a large tree in the right conditions.  The national champion of the species stands 124 feet high.	Specimen collected by Margaret Stones, Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew, 1976.<br><br>Acquisition of this drawing was sponsored by Mr. and Mrs. W. T. Hanna, Jr., in memory of Mr. and Mrs. W. T. Hanna and Mr. L. L. Morgan.<br><br>Margaret Stones is widely recognized as one of the foremost living botanical illustrators.  Born in 1920, in Melbourne, Australia, she moved to England in 1951 to study botanical illustration at the Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew, and in the course of a distinguished career became a principal illustrator for Kew Magazine and was selected as the artist for The Endemic Flora of Tasmania. Among numerous honors, she is a member of the Order of the British Empire and the Order of Australia; received from the Royal Horticultural Society the Veitch Silver Memorial Medal and the Veitch Gold Memorial Medal, and from the Garden Club of America the prestigious Eloise Payne Luquer Medal for special achievement in the field of botany; and holds honorary degrees from the University of Melbourne and LSU. <br><br>In 1976, Miss Stones was commissioned to create six watercolor drawings of Louisiana native flora to be a lasting legacy of LSU's bicentennial celebration. The LSU community was thrilled with the result, and the project soon blossomed with the support of people throughout Louisiana. By the time the project drew officially to a close in 1991, Miss Stones had created a major opus of more than 200 original watercolor drawings of Louisiana flora. The collection is unmatched in any other state.			Special Delivery: A Showcase of LSU Libraries Special Collections	E. A.
